## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / mechanical vibrations (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration and the inputs are time t and velocity v, which matches reduced-order oscillator/particle dynamics written as a first-order ODE dv/dt = f(t, v). With only v and t available (no position), the most likely structures are damping/drag, self-excitation (Rayleigh/Van-der-Pol-type), and external or parametric time-periodic forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Constant (bias) acceleration: dv_dt = c0 (uniform body force or constant drive)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * v (Stokes/viscous drag-dominated regime)
- Time-dependent bias forcing: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * t (slow ramp in applied force/drive)
- Harmonic (external) forcing: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) (periodic drive independent of state)
- Damped + harmonically forced (velocity-only reduced form): dv_dt = -c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3) (forced dissipative dynamics)
- Quadratic (turbulent) drag: dv_dt = -c0 * v * Abs(v) (high-Re drag scaling with v|v|)
- Cubic nonlinear damping: dv_dt = -c0 * v**3 (amplitude-dependent dissipation in nonlinear oscillations)
- Mixed linear+cubic damping: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * v**3 (captures low-speed viscous + high-speed nonlinear loss)
- Rayleigh/Van-der-Pol-type self-excitation (in v): dv_dt = (c0 - c1 * v**2) * v (negative damping at small |v| and positive damping at large |v| → limit cycle tendency)
- Saturating drag / smoothed Coulomb friction: dv_dt = -c0 * v / (Abs(v) + c1) (approaches constant-magnitude friction at large |v|)
- Time-modulated damping (parametric): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3)) * v (damping coefficient varies periodically in time)
- Forced nonlinear drag (combined effects): dv_dt = -c0 * v * Abs(v) + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3) (turbulent loss with periodic input)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd dependence on v (e.g., -c*v, -c*v**3) suggests dissipative forces opposing motion; the sign flips with v.
- A v*Abs(v) term is a strong indicator of quadratic/turbulent drag where dissipation grows ~v^2 and direction follows v.
- (c0 - c1*v**2)*v indicates negative damping near v=0 and positive damping at larger |v|, a hallmark of self-excited oscillators and limit-cycle regulation.
- Additive sin(c*t+phi) or cos(c*t+phi) terms typically represent external periodic forcing independent of the state.
- Multiplicative periodic factors with v, like cos(c*t)*v, point to parametric modulation (time-varying damping/gain), not just an external push.
- Rational saturation forms such as v/(Abs(v)+c) model friction/drag that approaches a bounded magnitude, mimicking dry friction with smoothing around v≈0.
- Higher odd powers (v**3, v**5) imply amplitude-dependent damping, producing faster decay at large speeds and slower decay near rest.
- If dv_dt depends primarily on t (weak v-dependence), the system behaves like a prescribed acceleration input rather than a strongly state-regulated oscillator.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO25)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v)
Candidate formulas: 54

GT is the fixed function
\[
0.938430539170744\,\sin(t)\;-\;0.866974142258927\,\sin(v).
\]
So any matching candidate must be expressible as “(constant)*sin(t) + (constant)*sin(v)” with **no extra nonzero terms**, and with the **t**-sine depending only on \(t\) (not \(v\)) and the **v**-sine depending only on \(v\) (not \(t\)). Phase shifts are allowed (e.g., \(\sin(t+\phi)\) can become \(\pm\sin(t)\) if \(\phi\in\{0,\pi\}\), or can become \(\cos(t)\) if \(\phi=\pi/2\), but GT is \(\sin\), so we’ll just choose phases that yield \(\sin\) with possible sign flips). Also any added polynomial/exp/log/abs terms must be set to zero via parameters; terms like “+ v” that have no parameter cannot be removed and therefore break equivalence.
